     3	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
     4	[37m      ** This program provides a Textual User Interface (TUI) to the **[39;49;00m$
     5	[37m      ** process of compiling and (optionally) executing an OpenCOBOL**[39;49;00m$
     6	[37m      ** program.                                                    **[39;49;00m$
     7	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
     8	[37m      ** This programs execution syntax is as follows:               **[39;49;00m$
     9	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    10	[37m      ** ocic <program-path-and-filename> [ <switch>... ]            **[39;49;00m$
    11	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    12	[37m      ** Once executed, a display screen will be presented showing   **[39;49;00m$
    13	[37m      ** the compilation options that will be used.  The user will   **[39;49;00m$
    14	[37m      ** have the opportunity to change options, specify new ones    **[39;49;00m$
    15	[37m      ** and specify any program execution arguments to be used if   **[39;49;00m$
    16	[37m      ** you select the "Execute" option.  When you press the Enter  **[39;49;00m$
    17	[37m      ** key the program will be compiled.                           **[39;49;00m$
    18	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    19	[37m      ** The SCREEN SECTION contains an image of the screen.         **[39;49;00m$
    20	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    21	[37m      ** The "010-Parse-Args" section in the PROCEDURE DIVISION has  **[39;49;00m$
    22	[37m      ** documentation on switches and their function.               **[39;49;00m$
    23	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
    24	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    25	[37m      ** AUTHOR:       GARY L. CUTLER                                **[39;49;00m$
    26	[37m      **               CutlerGL@gmail.com                            **[39;49;00m$
    27	[37m      **               Copyright (C) 2009-2010, Gary L. Cutler, GPL  **[39;49;00m$
    28	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    29	[37m      ** DATE-WRITTEN: June 14, 2009                                 **[39;49;00m$
    30	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
    31	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
    32	[37m      ** Note: Depending on which extended DISPLAY handler you're    **[39;49;00m$
    33	[37m      **       using (PDCurses, Curses, ...), you may need to un-    **[39;49;00m$
    34	[37m      **       comment any source lines tagged with "SCROLL" in cols **[39;49;00m$
    35	[37m      **       1-6 in order to have error messages scroll properly   **[39;49;00m$
    36	[37m      **       in the OCic shell window.                             **[39;49;00m$
    37	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$

    41	[37m      **        Is successful.  Also don't display messages if the   **[39;49;00m$
    42	[37m      **        output file is busy (just put a message on the       **[39;49;00m$
    43	[37m      **        screen, leave the OC screen up & let the user fix    **[39;49;00m$
    44	[37m      **        the problem & resubmit.                              **[39;49;00m$

    46	[37m      **        still cause the (old) executable to be launched.     **[39;49;00m$

   241	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$
   242	[37m      *> Here is the layout of the OCic screen.[39;49;00m$
   243	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$
   244	[37m      *> Note that this program can utilize the traditional PC line-drawing characters,[39;49;00m$
   245	[37m      *> if they are available.[39;49;00m$
   246	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$
   247	[37m      *> If this program is run on Windows, it must run with codepage 437 activated to[39;49;00m$
   248	[37m      *> display the line-drawing characters.  With a native Windows build or a[39;49;00m$
   249	[37m      *> Windows/MinGW build, one could use the command "chcp 437" to set that codepage[39;49;00m$
   250	[37m      *> for display within a Windows console window (that should be the default, though).[39;49;00m$
   251	[37m      *> With a Windows/Cygwin build, set the environment variable CYGWIN to a value of[39;49;00m$
   252	[37m      *> "codepage:oem" (this cannot be done from within the program though - you will[39;49;00m$
   253	[37m      *> have to use the "Computer/Advanced System Settings/Environment Variables" (Vista or[39;49;00m$
   254	[37m      *> Windows 7) function to define the variable.  XP Users: use "My Computer/Properties/[39;49;00m$
   255	[37m      *> Advanced/Environment Variables".[39;49;00m$
   256	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$
   257	[37m      *> To use OCic without the line-drawing characters, comment-out the first set of[39;49;00m$
   258	[37m      *> 78 "LD" items and uncomment the second.[39;49;00m$
   259	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$
   260	[37m      *> The following sample screen layout shows how the screen looks with line-drawing[39;49;00m$
   261	[37m      *> characters disabled.[39;49;00m$
   262	[37m      *>[39;49;00m$

   555	[34m                   [39;49;00m[33m'Error accessing file: "'[39;49;00m$
   556	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m             [39;49;00m[32mTRIM[39;49;00m([31mFile-Name[39;49;00m,[34mTRAILING[39;49;00m)$
   557	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m             [39;49;00m[33m'"'[39;49;00m$

   573	[37mGC0410[39;49;00m[37m             [39;49;00m[34mPERFORM[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m220[39;49;00m-[31mMake-Listing[39;49;00m$
   574	[37mGC0410[39;49;00m[37m         [39;49;00m[34mEND-IF[39;49;00m$
   575	[37mGC0709[39;49;00m[37m         [39;49;00m[34mIF  [39;49;00m([31mS-EXECUTE[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[35mNOT [39;49;00m=[37m [39;49;00m[31mSPACES[39;49;00m)$
   576	[37mGC0709[39;49;00m[37m         [39;49;00m[35mAND [39;49;00m([34m88[39;49;00m-[31mOutput-File-Avail[39;49;00m)$
   577	[37mGC0609[39;49;00m[37m             [39;49;00m[34mPERFORM[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m230[39;49;00m-[31mRun-Program[39;49;00m$

   582	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m009[39;49;00m-[31mDone[39;49;00m.$
   583	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mPERFORM[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m900[39;49;00m-[31mTerminate[39;49;00m$
   584	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m.$

   586	[37m      /[39;49;00m$
   587	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m010[39;49;00m-[31mParse-Args[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mSECTION[39;49;00m.$
   588	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   589	[37m      ** Process a sequence of KEYWORD=VALUE items.  These are items **[39;49;00m$
   590	[37m      ** specified on the command-line to provide the initial        **[39;49;00m$
   591	[37m      ** options shown selected on the screen.  When integrating     **[39;49;00m$
   592	[37m      ** OCic into an edirot or framework, include these switches on **[39;49;00m$
   593	[37m      ** the ocic.exe command the editor/framework executes.  Any    **[39;49;00m$
   594	[37m      ** underlined choice is the default value for that switch.     **[39;49;00m$
   595	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   596	[37m      ** @CONFIG=BS2000|COBOL85|COBOL2002|DEFAULT|IBM|MF|MVS         **[39;49;00m$
   597	[37m      **                                  =======                    **[39;49;00m$
   598	[37m      ** This switch specifies the default cobc compiler configura-  **[39;49;00m$
   599	[37m      ** tion file to be used                                        **[39;49;00m$
   600	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   601	[37m      ** @DEBUG=YES|NO                                               **[39;49;00m$
   602	[37m      **            ==                                               **[39;49;00m$
   603	[37m      ** This switch specifies whether (YES) or not (NO) debugging   **[39;49;00m$
   604	[37m      ** lines (those with a "D" in column 7) will be compiled.      **[39;49;00m$
   605	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   606	[37m      ** @DLL=YES|NO                                                 **[39;49;00m$
   607	[37m      **          ==                                                 **[39;49;00m$
   608	[37m      ** Use this switch to force ALL compiled programs to be built  **[39;49;00m$
   609	[37m      ** as DLLs ("@DLL=YES").  When main programs are built as DLLs **[39;49;00m$
   610	[37m      ** they must be executed using the cobcrun utility.  When      **[39;49;00m$
   611	[37m      ** "@DLL=NO" is in effect, main programs are generated as      **[39;49;00m$
   612	[37m      ** actual "exe" files and only subprograms will be generated   **[39;49;00m$
   613	[37m      ** as DLLs.                                                    **[39;49;00m$
   614	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   615	[37m      ** @EXECUTE=YES|NO                                             **[39;49;00m$
   616	[37m      **              ==                                             **[39;49;00m$
   617	[37m      ** This switch specifies whether ("@EXECUTE=YES") or not       **[39;49;00m$
   618	[37m      ** ("@EXECUTE=NO") the program will be executed after it is    **[39;49;00m$
   619	[37m      ** successfully compiled.                                      **[39;49;00m$
   620	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   621	[37m      ** @EXTRA=extra cobc argument(s)                               **[39;49;00m$
   622	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   623	[37m      ** This switch allows you to specify additional cobc arguments **[39;49;00m$
   624	[37m      ** that aren't managed by the other OC switches.  If used,     **[39;49;00m$
   625	[37m      ** this must be the last switch specified on the command line, **[39;49;00m$
   626	[37m      ** as everything that follows the "=" will be placed on the    **[39;49;00m$
   627	[37m      ** cobc command generated by OC.                               **[39;49;00m$
   628	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   629	[37m      ** @NOTRUNC=YES|NO                                             **[39;49;00m$
   630	[37m      **          ===                                                **[39;49;00m$
   631	[37m      ** This switch specifies whether (YES) or not (NO) the sup-    **[39;49;00m$
   632	[37m      ** pression of binary field truncation will occur.  If a PIC   **[39;49;00m$
   633	[37m      ** 99 COMP field (one byte of storage), for example, is given  **[39;49;00m$
   634	[37m      ** the value 123, it may have its value truncated to 23 when   **[39;49;00m$
   635	[37m      ** DISPLAYed.  Regardless of the NOTRUNC setting, internally   **[39;49;00m$
   636	[37m      ** the full precision of the field (allowing a maximum value   **[39;49;00m$
   637	[37m      ** of 255) will be preserved.  Even though truncation - if it  **[39;49;00m$
   638	[37m      ** does occur - would appear to have a minimal disruption on   **[39;49;00m$
   639	[37m      ** program operation, it has a significant effect on program   **[39;49;00m$
   640	[37m      ** run-time speed.                                             **[39;49;00m$
   641	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   642	[37m      ** @TRACE=YES|NO|ALL                                           **[39;49;00m$
   643	[37m      **            ==                                               **[39;49;00m$
   644	[37m      ** This switch controls whether or not code will be added to   **[39;49;00m$
   645	[37m      ** the object program to produce execution-time logic traces.  **[39;49;00m$
   646	[37m      ** A specification of "@TRACE=NO" means no such code will be   **[39;49;00m$
   647	[37m      ** produced.  By specifying "@TRACE=YES", code will be genera- **[39;49;00m$
   648	[37m      ** ted to display procedure names as they are entered.  A      **[39;49;00m$
   649	[37m      ** "@TRACE=ALL" specification will generate not only procedure **[39;49;00m$
   650	[37m      ** traces (as "@TRACE=YES" would) but also statement-level     **[39;49;00m$
   651	[37m      ** traces too!  All trace output is written to STDERR, so      **[39;49;00m$
   652	[37m      ** adding a "2>file" to the execution of the program will pipe **[39;49;00m$
   653	[37m      ** the trace output to a file.  You may find it valuable to    **[39;49;00m$
   654	[37m      ** add your own DISPLAY statements to the debugging output via **[39;49;00m$
   655	[37m      ** "DISPLAY xx UPON SYSERR"  The SYSERR device corresponds to  **[39;49;00m$
   656	[37m      ** the Windows or UNIX STDERR device and will therefore honor  **[39;49;00m$
   657	[37m      ** any "2>file" placed at the end of your program's execution. **[39;49;00m$
   658	[37m      ** Add a "D" in column 7 and you can control the generation or **[39;49;00m$
   659	[37m      ** ignoring of these DISPLAY statements via the "@DEBUG"       **[39;49;00m$
   660	[37m      ** switch.                                                     **[39;49;00m$
   661	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   662	[37mGC0410** @SOURCE=YES|NO                                              **[39;49;00m$
   663	[37mGC0410**           ==                                                **[39;49;00m$
   664	[37mGC0410** Use this switch to produce a source listing of the program, **[39;49;00m$
   665	[37mGC0410** PROVIDED it compiles without errors.                        **[39;49;00m$
   666	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
   667	[37mGC0410** @XREF=YES|NO                                                **[39;49;00m$
   668	[37mGC0410**           ==                                                **[39;49;00m$
   669	[37mGC0410** Use this switch to produce a cross-reference listing of the **[39;49;00m$
   670	[37mGC0410** program, PROVIDED it compiles without errors.               **[39;49;00m$
   671	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   672	$
   673	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m011[39;49;00m-[31mInit[39;49;00m.$

   685	[34m              [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mIF[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[31mSwitch-Keyword-And-Value[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[35mNOT [39;49;00m=[37m [39;49;00m[31mSPACES[39;49;00m$
   686	[31m                  [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mUNSTRING[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[31mSwitch-Keyword-And-Value[39;49;00m$
   687	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m                 [39;49;00m[34mDELIMITED[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mBY [39;49;00m[33m'='[39;49;00m$
   688	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m                 [39;49;00m[34mINTO[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[31mSwitch-Keyword[39;49;00m,[37m [39;49;00m[31mSwitch-Value[39;49;00m$
   689	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m             [39;49;00m[34mEND-UNSTRING[39;49;00m$
   690	[34m                  [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mPERFORM[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m030[39;49;00m-[31mProcess-Keyword[39;49;00m$
   691	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m         [39;49;00m[34mEND-IF[39;49;00m$

   693	[34m           [39;49;00m.$
   694	$
   695	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m019[39;49;00m-[31mDone[39;49;00m.$
   696	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mEXIT[39;49;00m.$
   697	$
   698	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   699	[37m      ** Since this program uses the SCREEN SECTION, it cannot do    **[39;49;00m$
   700	[37m      ** conventional console DISPLAY operations.  This routine      **[39;49;00m$
   701	[37m      ** (which, I admit, is like using an H-bomb to hunt rabbits)   **[39;49;00m$
   702	[37m      ** will submit an "ECHO" command to the system to simulate a   **[39;49;00m$
   703	[37m      ** DISPLAY.                                                    **[39;49;00m$
   704	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   705	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m021[39;49;00m-[31mBuild-And-Issue-Command[39;49;00m.$
   706	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mDISPLAY[39;49;00m$
   707	[34m              [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[31mOutput-Message[39;49;00m$
   708	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mEND-DISPLAY[39;49;00m$
   709	[34m           [39;49;00m.$
   710	$
   711	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m029[39;49;00m-[31mDone[39;49;00m.$
   712	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mEXIT[39;49;00m.$
   713	[37m      /[39;49;00m$
   714	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m030[39;49;00m-[31mProcess-Keyword[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34mSECTION[39;49;00m.$
   715	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   716	[37m      ** Process a single KEYWORD=VALUE item.                        **[39;49;00m$
   717	[37m      *****************************************************************[39;49;00m$
   718	$
   719	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[34m031[39;49;00m-[31mInit[39;49;00m.$
   720	[37m      [39;49;00m[37m     [39;49;00m[34mMOVE[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[32mUPPER-CASE[39;49;00m([31mSwitch-Keyword[39;49;00m)[37m [39;49;00m[34mTO[39;49;00m[37m [39;49;00m[31mSwitch-Keyword[39;49;00m$

  1755	[37m      ** This subprogram generates a cross-reference listing of an   **[39;49;00m$
  1756	[37m      ** OpenCOBOL program.                                          **[39;49;00m$
  1757	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
  1758	[37m      ** Linkage:      CALL "LISTING" USING <source>                 **[39;49;00m$
  1759	[37m      **                                    <xref>                   **[39;49;00m$
  1760	[37m      **                                    <filename>               **[39;49;00m$
  1761	[37m      **                                                             **[39;49;00m$
  1762	[37m      **               Where:                                        **[39;49;00m$
  1763	[37m      **                  <source>   is a PIC X(1) flag indicating   **[39;49;00m$
  1764	[37m      **                             whether or not a source listing **[39;49;00m$
  1765	[37m      **                             should be produced (space=NO,   **[39;49;00m$
  1766	[37m      **                             non-space=yes)                  **[39;49;00m$
  1767	[37m      **                  <xref>     is a PIC X(1) flag indicating   **[39;49;00m$
  1768	[37m      **                             whether or not an xref listing  **[39;49;00m$
  1769	[37m      **                             should be produced (space=NO,   **[39;49;00m$
  1770	[37m      **                             non-space=yes)                  **[39;49;00m$
  1771	[37m      **                  <filename> is the [path]filename of the    **[39;49;00m$
  1772	[37m      **                             program being listed and/or     **[39;49;00m$
  1773	[37m      **                             xreffed in a PIC X(256) form.   **[39;49;00m$
